<link href="LEX_US.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <link href="OELD_font.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <link href="OELD_sound.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_config.ini"></script> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_jquery.js"></script> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_script.js"></script> <div class="OELDBody"><div class="entryWrapper world"><div class="entryHead primary_homograph" id="abacost"><div class="entryTable"><div class="entryWord first"><h1>Definition of <em>abacost</em> in English:</h1> <h2 class="hwg"><span class="hw" >abacost</span></h2><div class="variant">(also <strong>abacos</strong>)</div></div><div class="entryLogo"><div class="container"> </div></div></div></div><section class="pronun"><span class="pron inline"><span class="phoneticSymbol">/ˈabəkɒst/</span> </span></section><section class="gramb"><h3 class="ps pos"><span class="pos">noun</span></h3><span class="transitivity"></span><ul class="semb"><li><div class="trg"><p><span class="iteration"></span><span class="same">☆</span><span class="ind">In the Democratic Republic of the Congo (formerly Zaire): a man's suit consisting of a short-sleeved collarless jacket and loose trousers.</span></p><p class="note"><span class="same">☆</span>The wearing of shirts and ties was outlawed by President Mobutu for the majority of his time in power (1965–97), as symbolic of the country's colonial past, and the abacost promoted as the national costume and worn by his supporters. The abacost was also adopted as official costume in the 1970s by some other African countries.</p><span class="indicators"></span></div></li></ul></section><section class="etymology etym origin active"><h3><strong>Origin</strong><div class="sectionswitch"> <span class="switchbutton"> <span class="switchbuttonline center"></span><span class="switchbuttonline top"></span><span class="switchbuttonline bottom"></span></span></div></h3><div class="senseInnerWrapper"><p>1970s; earliest use found in The New York Times. From African French (Congo) abacost, abacos, apparently shortened from the French slogan à bas le costume, lit. ‘down with the (Western) suit’ from à bas down, downwards + le, masculine definite article + costume suit.</p></div></section> <div class="oeldToolbar middle line logoColor" > <div class="line left">&nbsp;</div> <div class="otLogo"> <div class="otContainer"></div> </div> <div class="otToolbox"> </div> <div class="line right">&nbsp;</div> </div> </div><span class="LEXUKey" key="abacost" style="display:none !important"></span></div>
</>
abacot
<link href="LEX_US.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <link href="OELD_font.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <link href="OELD_sound.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_config.ini"></script> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_jquery.js"></script> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_script.js"></script> <div class="OELDBody"><div class="entryWrapper world"><div class="entryHead primary_homograph" id="abacot"><div class="entryTable"><div class="entryWord first"><h1>Definition of <em>abacot</em> in English:</h1> <h2 class="hwg"><span class="hw" >abacot</span></h2></div><div class="entryLogo"><div class="container"> </div></div></div></div><section class="pronun"><span class="pron inline"><span class="phoneticSymbol">/ˈabəkɒt/</span> </span></section><section class="gramb"><h3 class="ps pos"><span class="pos">noun</span></h3><span class="transitivity"></span><span class="sense-registers">rare </span><ul class="semb"><li><div class="trg"><p><span class="iteration"></span><span class="same">☆</span><span class="ind">Bycoket.</span></p><p class="note"><span class="same">☆</span>Originally only with reference to the bycocket worn by Henry VI, but by the 18th century apparently perceived to denote a king's bycocket more generally, and by the 19th century no longer restricted to royalty.</p><span class="indicators"></span></div></li></ul></section><section class="etymology etym origin active"><h3><strong>Origin</strong><div class="sectionswitch"> <span class="switchbutton"> <span class="switchbuttonline center"></span><span class="switchbuttonline top"></span><span class="switchbuttonline bottom"></span></span></div></h3><div class="senseInnerWrapper"><p>Mid 16th century; earliest use found in Hall's Vnion. Apparently originally a misprint for bycoket, incorporating a preceding indefinite article, unless reflecting an actual spoken variant with attraction of the indefinite article; subsequently shortened by Holinshed, and altered again in a later edition of Holinshed's text, perhaps as a result of misreading of the form abacoc forms (although this is apparently first attested later). Subsequently popularized by dictionaries ultimately informed by editions of Holinshed.</p></div></section> <div class="oeldToolbar middle line logoColor" > <div class="line left">&nbsp;</div> <div class="otLogo"> <div class="otContainer"></div> </div> <div class="otToolbox"> </div> <div class="line right">&nbsp;</div> </div> </div><span class="LEXUKey" key="abacot" style="display:none !important"></span></div>

<link href="LEX_US.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <link href="OELD_font.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <link href="OELD_sound.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_config.ini"></script> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_jquery.js"></script> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_script.js"></script> <div class="OELDBody"><div class="entryWrapper world"><div class="entryHead primary_homograph" id="abaisance"><div class="entryTable"><div class="entryWord first"><h1>Definition of <em>abaisance</em> in English:</h1> <h2 class="hwg"><span class="hw" >abaisance</span></h2></div><div class="entryLogo"><div class="container"> </div></div></div></div><section class="pronun"><span class="pron inline"><span class="phoneticSymbol">/əˈbeɪ(ɪ)sns/</span> </span></section><section class="gramb"><h3 class="ps pos"><span class="pos">noun</span></h3><span class="transitivity"></span><span class="sense-registers">rare </span><ul class="semb"><li><div class="trg"><p><span class="iteration"></span><span class="same">☆</span><span class="ind">An act expressing deference or respect, usually a bending forwards of the body; a bow.</span></p><span class="indicators"></span></div></li></ul></section><section class="etymology etym origin active"><h3><strong>Origin</strong><div class="sectionswitch"> <span class="switchbutton"> <span class="switchbuttonline center"></span><span class="switchbuttonline top"></span><span class="switchbuttonline bottom"></span></span></div></h3><div class="senseInnerWrapper"><p>Late 15th century; earliest use found in Ordinances Chivalry. From Middle French abessance, abesance abasement, humility from abaissant, present participle of abaisser to lower, humiliate: see -ance.</p></div></section> <div class="oeldToolbar middle line logoColor" > <div class="line left">&nbsp;</div> <div class="otLogo"> <div class="otContainer"></div> </div> <div class="otToolbox"> </div> <div class="line right">&nbsp;</div> </div> </div><span class="LEXUKey" key="abaisance" style="display:none !important"></span></div>

abaiser
<link href="LEX_US.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <link href="OELD_font.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <link href="OELD_sound.css" rel="stylesheet" type="text/css"> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_config.ini"></script> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_jquery.js"></script> <script type="text/javascript" src="OELD_script.js"></script> <div class="OELDBody"><div class="entryWrapper world"><div class="entryHead primary_homograph" id="abaiser"><div class="entryTable"><div class="entryWord first"><h1>Definition of <em>abaiser</em> in English:</h1> <h2 class="hwg"><span class="hw" >abaiser</span></h2></div><div class="entryLogo"><div class="container"> </div></div></div></div><section class="pronun"><span class="pron inline"><span class="phoneticSymbol">/əˈbeɪsə/</span> </span></section><section class="gramb"><h3 class="ps pos"><span class="pos">noun</span></h3><span class="transitivity"></span><ul class="semb"><li><div class="trg"><p><span class="iteration"></span><span class="same">☆</span><span class="ind">A soft black pigment; ivory black, bone black.</span></p><p class="note"><span class="same">☆</span>Recorded chiefly in dictionaries.</p><span class="indicators"></span></div></li></ul></section><section class="etymology etym origin active"><h3><strong>Origin</strong><div class="sectionswitch"> <span class="switchbutton"> <span class="switchbuttonline center"></span><span class="switchbuttonline top"></span><span class="switchbuttonline bottom"></span></span></div></h3><div class="senseInnerWrapper"><p>Mid 19th century; earliest use found in John Weale (1791–1862), publisher and writer on architecture. Apparently from French abaisser (in painting) to tone down the intensity of a colour by using black alongside, specific use of abaisser to reduce in intensity.</p></div></section> <div class="oeldToolbar middle line logoColor" > <div class="line left">&nbsp;</div> <div class="otLogo"> <div class="otContainer"></div> </div> <div class="otToolbox"> </div> <div class="line right">&nbsp;</div> </div> </div><span class="LEXUKey" key="abaiser" style="display:none !important"></span></div>
